          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





Please provide a brief explanation of the security issue.



<b class="line"><!---->Please provide a brief explanation of the security issue.<!----></b>



<br>





In 



<span class="line"><!---->In <!----></span>





https://crrev.com/c/3186434



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3186434"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3186434<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 it added the special handling of class constructors. The check for class constructors was moved to Call, so when the target of CallFunction is constructor, it will call constructor rather than raise an error.



<span class="line"><!----> it added the special handling of class constructors. The check for class constructors was moved to Call, so when the target of CallFunction is constructor, it will call constructor rather than raise an error.<!----></span>



<br>





In `JSCallReducer::ReduceJSCall`, it has a branch which recude the case which target is kJSCreateClosure[2]. When the sfi is ClassConstructor kind, the Call will be reduce into CallRuntime(Runtime::kThrowConstructorNonCallableError). But when the `broker()->StackHasOverflowed()`, it won't do that.



<span class="line"><!---->In `JSCallReducer::ReduceJSCall`, it has a branch which recude the case which target is kJSCreateClosure[2]. When the sfi is ClassConstructor kind, the Call will be reduce into CallRuntime(Runtime::kThrowConstructorNonCallableError). But when the `broker()-&gt;StackHasOverflowed()`, it won't do that.<!----></span>



<br>

And the `CallFunction_ReceiverIsNullOrUndefined` will call `CallFunction`. So after the optimization, it will call a constructor.



<span class="line"><!---->And the `CallFunction_ReceiverIsNullOrUndefined` will call `CallFunction`. So after the optimization, it will call a constructor.<!----></span>



<br>





```c++



<span class="line"><!---->```c++<!----></span>



<br>





void Builtins::Generate_CallFunction_ReceiverIsNullOrUndefined(



<span class="line"><!---->void Builtins::Generate_CallFunction_ReceiverIsNullOrUndefined(<!----></span>



<br>





    MacroAssembler* masm) {



<span class="line"><!---->    MacroAssembler* masm) {<!----></span>



<br>





  Generate_CallFunction(masm, ConvertReceiverMode::kNullOrUndefined);



<span class="line"><!---->  Generate_CallFunction(masm, ConvertReceiverMode::kNullOrUndefined);<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





Since the different between `Builtins::Generate_CallFunction` and `Generate_Construct`, it will cause many unexception case such as type confusion in attached file.



<span class="line"><!---->Since the different between `Builtins::Generate_CallFunction` and `Generate_Construct`, it will cause many unexception case such as type confusion in attached file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I notice it addes check at ReduceJSCallWithArrayLike and ReduceJSCallWithSpread to prevent the target of CallFunction is Construct in 



<span class="line"><!---->I notice it addes check at ReduceJSCallWithArrayLike and ReduceJSCallWithSpread to prevent the target of CallFunction is Construct in <!----></span>

Add check for class constructor to CallFunction



<span class="line"><!---->Add check for class constructor to CallFunction<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Raise an exception if CallFunction is invoked with a class constructor.



<span class="line"><!---->Raise an exception if CallFunction is invoked with a class constructor.<!----></span>



<br>





The check was initially removed in [1] but there are cases where we



<span class="line"><!---->The check was initially removed in [1] but there are cases where we<!----></span>



<br>





could end in CallFunction with class constructors from optimized code.



<span class="line"><!---->could end in CallFunction with class constructors from optimized code.<!----></span>

Merged: Add check for class constructor to CallFunction



<span class="line"><!---->Merged: Add check for class constructor to CallFunction<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Raise an exception if CallFunction is invoked with a class constructor.



<span class="line"><!---->Raise an exception if CallFunction is invoked with a class constructor.<!----></span>



<br>





The check was initially removed in [1] but there are cases where we



<span class="line"><!---->The check was initially removed in [1] but there are cases where we<!----></span>



<br>





could end in CallFunction with class constructors from optimized code.



<span class="line"><!---->could end in CallFunction with class constructors from optimized code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

          text-decoration: underline;
        }

          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
